Congruence	Congruence If two numbers and have the property that their
difference is integrally divisible by a number (i.e., is an integer),
then and are said to be "congruent modulo ." The number is called the
modulus, and the statement " is congruent to (modulo )" is written
mathematically as                                                   
                                                 (1)
                                                   If is not integrally
divisible by , then it is said that " is not congruent to (modulo ),"
which is written                                                   
                                                 (2)
                                                   The explicit "(mod )"
is sometimes omitted when the modulus is understood by context, so in
such cases, care must be taken not to confuse the symbol with the
equivalence sign. The quantity is sometimes called the "base," and the
quantity is called the residue or remainder. There are several types of
residues. The common residue defined to be nonnegative and smaller than
, while the minimal residue is or , whichever is smaller in absolute
value. Congruence arithmetic is perhaps most familiar as a
generalization of the arithmetic of the clock. Since there are 60
minutes in an hour, "minute arithmetic" uses a modulus of . If one
starts at 40 minutes past the hour and then waits another 35 minutes, ,
so the current time would be 15 minutes past the (next) hour.

가정법	◆ 가정법 ◆ 1. 가정법 기본 공식 ① 가정법 현재 ( 현재[미래]의 불확
실한 가정 ) IF절 : If + S + V현재시제 ~, 주절 : S + will + 동원 ~ / 명령
문   ② 가정법 미래 ( 미래의 강한 의심 ) IF절 : If + S + should + 동원 ~,
주절 : 명령문 S + can[may/will/shall/would] 동원   ③ 가정법 과거 ( 현재
사실의 반대로 가정 ) IF절 : If + S + V과거시제 ~, 주절 : S +
would[could/should/might] 동원   ④ 가정법 과거완료 ( 과거 사실의 반대로
가정 ) IF절 : If + S + had + p.p ~, 주절 : S + would[could/should/might]
+ have + p.p ~.   [1] 가정법 현재 ( ~ 한다면, ~ 할텐데 ) (1) If major
shopping malls discount prices by 35 percent, most of the small stores
will go bankrupt.   (2) If you experience any trouble with your new
electronic appliance, please consult the user's manual.   [2] 가정법 미
래 ( ~ 한다면, ~ 할텐데 ) => 도치 ( Should + 주 + 동원 ~ ) (1) If you
should need further assistance, I would recommend calling your
supervisor.   (2) If you should need to use a fax machine during your
stay, please contact the Business Center in our hotel.   [3] 가정법 과거
( ~ 한다면, ~ 할텐데 ) (1) If more suburban commuters lived closer to
train stations, they would drive their vehicles much less frequently.  
[4] 가정법 과거완료 => ( ~ 했었다면, ~ 했었을 텐데 ) => 도치 ( Had + 주
+ p.p ~ ) (1) If they had known the correct number of participants in
advance, they could have prepared more adequate materials.   [5] 혼합가
정법 => If절의 내용은 과거 => 주절의 내용은 현재 * If you had not taken
my advice, you would have been in trouble now. => would be   2. If 대용
어구 ① without + 명사 [ 가정법 과거 ] (현재 ~ 이 없다면 / 아니라면, 현재
... 할텐데) = If it were not for + 명사 = Were it not for + 명사 = If
not for + 명사 = But for + 명사 = Except for + 명사 Ex) We would fail in
winning the Metrocom account without Tom Hank's exceptional effort and
dedication.   [ 가정법 과거완료 ] ( 과거 ~ 이 없었다면 / 아니었다면, 과
거에 ... 했었을 텐데 ) = If it had not been for + 명사 = Had it not been
for + 명사 = if not for + 명사 = But for + 명사 = Except for + 명사 Ex)
Without your help, I would never have succeeded in establishing my
institute.   ② provided ( = providing ) that + S + V : ~ 한다면 Ex) Your
lost personal belongings can be returned to you, provided that they are
proven to be yours.   ③ in case (that) + S + V : ~ 할 경우를 대비해서
Ex) Please provide a close relative or friend's cellular phone number in
case there is an emergency. ④ as long as ( = so long as = only if ) ~ 하
는 한 (최소한의 조건) Ex) You can take tomorrow off as long as you can
complete the job on time.   3. Should가 생략된 가정법 현재의 명사절 아래
에 제시된 동사 및 형용사는 현재 or 미래에 대한 당위성을 말하며 that절 이
하에서 [ should + 동사원형 ]에서 조동사 should가 생략되므로, 반드시 동사
는 동사원형이 되어야 한다.   ① S + 주장/명령/충고/요구/제안의 동사 +
that + S + (should) + 동사원형 주장 : insist, urge 명령 : order,
command, mandate 충고 : advise, recommend 요구 : ask, demand, request,
require 제안 : suggest, propose, move   Ex) Students have requested that
the results of the mid-term be posted on the bulletin board.   ② It is +
이성/감정적 판단의 형용사 + that + S + (should) + 동사원형   important,
imperative, essential, crucial necessary, natural, urgent, (im)possible,
vital, advisable, desirable, sorry, strange   Ex) When you wish to buy a
used car, it is important that it be test-driven first. ◆ 도치 ◆ [1] 부
정어의 도치 : 부정어 ( never / seldom / scarcely / not only / hardly /
rarely ) 강조를 위해 문장의 어순이 바뀐다. => 부정어 + 동사 + 주어 ● 주
어 + be동사 => be동사 + 주어 ● 주어 + 조동사 + 동사원형 => 조동사 + 주어
+ 동사원형 ● 주어 + 일반동사 => do / does / did + 주어 + 동사원형 ● 주어
+ have / has / had + p.p => have / has / had + 주어 + p.p Ex) Ms. Jane's
poor eyesight never interfered with her ability to read student
writings.   => Never did Ms. Jane's poor eyesight interfere with her
ability to read student writings.   [2] [ No sooner had + 주어 + p.p
than + 주어 + 과거동사 ] 〓 [ Hardly / Scarcely had + 주어 + p.p when /
before + 주어 + 과거동사 ] 〓 [ As soon as + 주어 + 과거동사 ~ , 주어 +
과거동사 ~ ] : ~ 하자마자 ~ 했다   Ex) No sooner had Mr. Barnet left for
the day than the phone rang.   = Hardly / Scarcely had Mr. Barnet left
for the day when / before the phone rang.   = As soon as Mr. Barnet left
for the day, the phone rang.   [3] 동의를 나타내는 표현 (1) 부정적 동의
[ neither / nor + be동사 / 조동사 + 주어 ] : 나 역시 ~ 않다 Ex) The
sales manager couldn't join the general staff meeting and neither could
the accounting manager.   (2) 긍정적 동의 [ so + be동사/조동사 + 주어 ]
: 나 또한 ~ 이다 Ex) I enjoy romantic movies. ― So do I.   [4] 부정적 의
미의 부사(구)가 문장 앞에 올 때 Not ... until ~ ( ~ 해서야 비로소 ... 하
다 ) In no way ( 결코 ~ 않다 ) Not even[once] ( (한번도) ~ 조차 않다 )
Not only ~ but also.. ( ~뿐만 아니라 ..도 ) Under no circumstances ( 어
떤 일이 있더라도 ~ 않다 / 결코 ~ 아니다 ) Little ( 전혀 ~ 않다 ) Ex) Not
until I saw him in person I realized how tall he was. => Not until I saw
him in person did I realize how tall he was.   [5] 가정법의 도치 ① 가정
법 미래 If you should meet John, please give him my best regards. =>
Should you meet John, please give him my best regards. ② 가정법 과거완료
If he had been invited, he would have come. => Had he been invited, he
would have come.   [6] There / Here + 동사 + 주어 Ex) Here comes the
bus! There goes the bus!   [주의] 주어가 대명사 일 때는 어순이 변경 안됨
Ex) Here it comes! / There it comes!

noteworthy shape to objects of that kind.

Gandhi\'s Shoes	Gandhi's Shoes   As Gandhi stepped aboard a train one
day, one of his shoes slipped off and landed on the track. He was unable
to retrieve it as the train started rolling. To the amazement of his
companions, Gandhi calmly took off his other shoe and threw it back
along the track to land close to the first shoe. Asked by a fellow
passenger why he did that, Gandhi replied, 'the poor man who finds the
shoe lying on the track will now have a pair he can use.'

특징, 눈에 띄는 점
The police are	"The police is" or "The police are"? For example, The
police is after me. The police are after me. I guess the strictly
correct answer should be "are" since it's a plural word, but for some
reason I tend to write "is" when I'm not thinking about it, indicating
that's the version I most commonly read.                         3
Answers Andrew Meyer, a native speaker of American English 4.6k Views
You are correct. The phrase "the police are" is grammatically correct,
whereas "the police is" is not. This is because "police" is plural. You
could say "the police department is" because "police department" is
singular, but that's beside the point. As for whether "the police is" is
a commonly used phrase, I'm not really sure. Google Ngram Viewer
suggests that "the police are" has been used much more commonly in
recent history. Written Jan 2, 2013 · View Upvotes

in hot water ( = in a difficult situation )	in hot water Also found in:
Dictionary. Related to in hot water: at the eleventh hour *in hot water
(with someone) (about someone or something) Fig. in trouble.
(*Typically: be ~; get [into] ~.) You are going to get into hot water
with Rebecca about that. Amy got into hot water about Todd with Rebecca.
John got himself into hot water by being late. See also: hot, water

The McGraw-Hill Companies, Inc. in hot water in a difficult situation in

Financial, Idioms, Encyclopedia, Wikipedia. ThesaurusAntonymsRelated
WordsSynonymsLegend: Switch to new thesaurus                          
                        Verb                         1.
                        go far - succeed in a big way; get to the top;
"After he published his book, he had arrived"; "I don't know whether I
can make it in science!"; "You will go far, my boy!"
                        arrive, get in, make it
                        bring home the bacon, deliver the goods,
succeed, win, come through - attain success or reach a desired goal;
"The enterprise succeeded"; "We succeeded in getting tickets to the
show"; "she struggled to overcome her handicap and won"
                                                          
                                                  2.
                        go far - extend in importance or range; "His
accomplishments go far"                         go deep
                        extend, run, lead, pass, go - stretch out over a
distance, space, time, or scope; run or extend between two points or
beyond a certain point; "Service runs all the way to Cranbury"; "His
knowledge doesn't go very far"; "My memory extends back to my fourth
year of life"; "The facts extend beyond a consideration of her personal
assets"                                                    Based on

wade through	wade through Also found in: Dictionary. wade through
something   1. to walk with effort through a substance, such as water,
mud, garbage, etc. The soldiers waded through the mud on the way to
battle. They waded through the mess to get to where they were going. 2.
Fig. to struggle through something with difficulty. (Fig. on {2}.) You
mean I have to wade through all these applications? I have to wade
through forty term papers in the next two days. See also: wade

swear someone in (as something)	swear someone in (as something) to
administer an oath to someone who then officially begins in office. The
judge swore Alice in as street commissioner. The judge swore in Alice as
the new director.
\"you lost me\"	"you lost me" means that you do not understand what the
speaker is saying. Sometimes it could be because his story has become
too long and elaborate, or perhaps he is talking about a topic you know
nothing about. It's not impolite to say "I'm sorry, but you lost me
there" or something similar, and using such an idiom will in fact make
you sound more like a native speaker.
dump on	Also found in: Dictionary. dump on someone or something   1. .
to snow on someone or something. Well, it dumped on us again last night.
The cold front dumped on the northeast again today. 2. and do a dump on
someone or something; dump all over someone or something S(. to
criticize someone or something; to destroy someone or something. There
is no need to do a dump on me. I didn't wreck your car. The boss?mad as
a wet hen?dumped all over me. See also: dump dump something on someone
Fig. to pour out one's troubles to someone. She dumped all her grief on
her friend, Sally. I wish you wouldn't dump all your problems on me.

Be my guest 스스로 돕다	Be my guest. Help yourself.; After you. (A
polite way of indicating that someone else should go first, help himself
or herself to something, or take the last one of something.) Mary: I
would just love to have some more cake, but there is only one piece
left. Sally: Be my guest. Mary: Wow! Thanks! Jane: Here's the door. Who
should go in first? Bill: Be my guest. I'll wait out here. Jane: You're
so polite!

in abundance 풍족한	a·bun·dance  (?-b?n′d?ns) n. 1. a. A great or
plentiful amount: an abundance of rain. b. The condition of being in
rich supply: bananas growing in abundance. 2. a. Degree of
plentifulness: "Species of low abundance are ignored in the calculation
of predominance" (William M. Lewis). b. Chemistry The amount of an
isotope of an element that exists in nature, usually expressed as a
percentage of the total amount of all isotopes of the element. 3.
Affluence; prosperity: living in abundance.

cool down 열을 식히다, 화를 가라앉히다	cool down Also found in:
Dictionary, Thesaurus, Medical, Legal, Encyclopedia, Wikipedia. cool
someone down  and cool someone off  1. Lit. to cool someone by reducing
the heat or applying something cold. Here, have a cold drink. Cool
yourself down. The ice finally cooled down the feverish child. We need
to cool off the pudding in a hurry. 2. Fig. to reduce someone's anger.
(Reducing the "heat" of anger.) I just stared at him while he was
yelling. I knew that would cool him down. The coach talked to them for a
long time. That cooled them off. 3. Fig. to reduce someone's passion or
love. (Reducing the "heat" of passion.) When she slapped him, that
really cooled him down. Seeing Mary was too intense, so Bill cooled
himself off by breaking it off for a while.

to attain some goal, such as a victory in a contest: The top three
students in the class vied for the title of valedictorian.

pay one\'s dues 권한을 얻다	pay one's dues   1. Lit. to pay the fees
required to belong to an organization. If you haven't paid your dues,
you can't come to the club picnic. How many people have paid their dues?
2. Fig. to have earned one's right to something through hard work or
suffering. He worked hard to get to where he is today. He paid his dues
and did what he was told. I have every right to be here. I paid my dues!
See also: due, pay McGraw-Hill Dictionary of American Idioms and Phrasal
Verbs. ? 2002 by The McGraw-Hill Companies, Inc. pay your dues to earn
respect because you worked hard to develop a skill She paid her dues
playing in small clubs in New York before an album made her famous.

with respect to something	with respect to someone or something of or
about someone or something. With respect to radiation, this power plant
is very safe. This article examines experiments with respect to ethical
issues. See also: respect McGraw-Hill Dictionary of American Idioms and
Phrasal Verbs. ? 2002 by The McGraw-Hill Companies, Inc. with respect to
something (slightly formal) also in respect to something considering or
relating to something with regard to something There is another question
with respect to this plan that must be answered before any decision can
be made. Do you really believe your memory is clear in respect to what
happened? Related vocabulary: in terms of something See also: respect

pick something up	pick something up   1. Lit. to lift up or raise
something from a lower place. Please help me pick this stuff up off the
pavement. Pick up every bit of it! 2. Fig. to tidy up or clean up a room
or some other place. Let's pick this room up in a hurry. I want you to
pick up the entire house. 3. Fig. to find, purchase, or acquire
something. Where did you pick that up? I picked up this tool at the
hardware store. 4. Fig. to learn something. I pick languages up easily.
I picked up a lot of knowledge about music from my brother. 5. Fig. to
cause something to go faster, especially music. All right, let's pick up
the tempo and get it moving faster. Okay, get moving. Pick it up! 6.
Fig. to resume something. Pick it up right where you stopped. I'll have
to pick up my work where I left off. 7. Fig. to receive radio signals;
to bring something into view. I can just pick it up with a powerful
telescope. I can hardly pick up a signal. 8. Fig. to find a trail or
route. The dogs finally picked the scent up. You should pick up highway
80 in a few miles. See also: pick, up

blow up 폭발하다	blow up   1. Lit. [for something] to explode. The bomb
might have blown up if the children had tried to move it. The
firecracker blew up. 2. Fig. to burst into anger. I just knew you'd blow
up. So she blew up. Why should that affect you so much? 3. Fig. an angry
outburst; a fight. (Usually blowup.) After the third blowup, she left
him. One blowup after another from you. Control your temper! 4. Fig. an
enlarged version of a photograph, map, chart, etc. (Usually blowup.)
Here's a blowup of the scene of the crime. Kelly sent a blowup of their
wedding picture to all her relatives. 5. Fig. the ruination of
something; the collapse of something. (Usually blowup.) The blowup in
the financial world has ruined my chances for early retirement. After
the blowup at the company, the top managers called one another to
compare notes. 6. Fig. to fall apart or get ruined. The whole project
blew up. It will have to be canceled. All my planning was blown up this
afternoon. 7. [for a storm] to arrive accompanied by the blowing of the
wind. A terrible storm blew up while we were in the movie theater. I was
afraid that a rainstorm was blowing up.

take it on the chin	take it on the chin  and take it on the nose  1.
Lit. to stand up to something adverse, such as criticism. (Fig. on
taking a direct punch to the head in boxing.) They laid some blunt
criticism on him, but he took it on the chin. I knew he could take it on
the nose. 2. Fig. to receive the full brunt of something. Why do I have
to take it on the chin for something I didn't do? If you did it, you
have to learn to take it on the chin.

Fig. to act better than one really is; to pretend to be good or to be
superior. Pay no attention to her. She is just putting on airs. Stop
giving yourself airs and act like the rest of us. See also: air, on, put

doubt (something) His report calls into doubt the earlier reports we
had.

occur, especially in a formal or threatening manner.

change of trade policy’
